</file_contents>
<user_instructions>
<taskname="HH Pareto Prompt"/>
<task>
Draft a ready-to-paste ChatGPT / GPT-Pro prompt export that defines the staged Hubbard-Holstein workflow tradeoff problem in this repo before proposing any solution. The export should ask GPT-Pro to formalize the problem statement, define the comparison unit (what counts as a workflow or workflow policy), define the Pareto / nondominance setup, identify the right objective dimensions and constraints, and establish evaluation vocabulary for comparing workflows. Do not ask GPT-Pro to redesign repo architecture or recommend implementations yet. The export should stay HH-first and repo-native.

The export should explicitly cover:
- warm-start `hh_hva_ptw`;
- staged ADAPT pool/curriculum choices such as `paop_lf_std`, `hva`, `full_meta`, and related family/residual distinctions;
- continuation modes `legacy`, `phase1_v1`, `phase2_v1`, `phase3_v1`;
- handoff / replay behavior via `match_adapt` with `full_meta` fallback;
- budget/control knobs such as `max_depth`, optimizer `nfev`, replay depth / parameter count, and shot / measurement burden;
- hardware-cost proxies such as `cx_proxy_total` and `depth_proxy_total`;
- the difference between search/discovery cost and final compiled / executed cost.

The next model’s output should be the external prompt text only, formatted cleanly with XML tags and light markdown. A good export will likely ask GPT-Pro to define sections such as problem statement, repo facts, decision variables, objectives, constraints, Pareto definition, fairness/comparability rules, evaluation vocabulary, and open framing questions.
</task>

<architecture>
- `AGENTS.md`, `README.md`, `pipelines/run_guide.md`, `MATH/Math.md`, and `MATH/IMPLEMENT_SOON.md` define the policy boundary and vocabulary: HH-first, warm-start -> staged ADAPT -> replay, `phase3_v1` as canonical continuation default, depth-0 narrow core `paop_lf_std`, `full_meta` as residual enrichment / replay fallback, and energy-drop-first continuation logic.
- `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_staged_cli_args.py` and `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_staged_workflow.py` define staged HH defaults and budgets: warm ansatz defaults to `hh_hva_ptw`; replay defaults to `generator_family=match_adapt`, `fallback_family=full_meta`; replay continuation mode follows ADAPT mode unless overridden; scaled defaults tie `warm_reps`, `adapt_max_depth`, `adapt_maxiter`, `final_reps`, and trajectory settings to `L`.
- `pipelines/hardcoded/adapt_pipeline.py`, `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_scoring.py`, `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_stage_control.py`, and `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_types.py` define the staged ADAPT selection surface: pool families, `simple_v1` / `full_v2` scoring, stage gating, compile / measurement / lifetime cost terms, and stop-policy defaults.
- `pipelines/hardcoded/handoff_state_bundle.py`, `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_replay.py`, `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_generators.py`, and `pipelines/hardcoded/hh_vqe_from_adapt_family.py` define the handoff / replay contract: provenance-aware generator-family resolution, seed policies, phase-specific replay controllers, and fallback behavior when `match_adapt` cannot be resolved.
- `pipelines/exact_bench/benchmark_metrics_proxy.py`, `pipelines/exact_bench/hh_l2_stage_unit_audit_workflow.py`, `pipelines/exact_bench/hh_l2_logical_screen_workflow.py`, `pipelines/exact_bench/hh_fixed_handoff_replay_optimizer_probe_workflow.py`, and `pipelines/exact_bench/hh_full_pool_expressivity_probe_workflow.py` provide existing comparison surfaces for stage-local contribution, multi-point workflow robustness, optimizer sensitivity under fixed scaffold, and scaffold-free full-pool expressivity.
- `docs/reports/qiskit_circuit_report.py` and `pipelines/exact_bench/hh_noise_robustness_seq_report.py` carry the repo’s hardware-proxy and runtime/measurement reporting vocabulary: `term_exp_count_total`, `pauli_rot_count_total`, `cx_proxy_total`, `sq_proxy_total`, `depth_proxy_total`, `wall_total_s`, `oracle_eval_s_total`, and `oracle_calls_total`.
- `artifacts 1/useful/L2/20260309_plateau_v3_summary.md` and `L2_hh_smart_replay.md` are concrete on-disk evidence artifacts showing that workflow accuracy, replay depth, `nfev`, and fallback-family behavior can move differently.
- `prompt-exports/2026-03-13-0010-plan-hh-sweep-experiments.md` and `prompt-exports/2026-03-12-2359-plan-hh-operator-pool-expansion.md` are style/examples for the kind of external-model prompt export the next model should produce.
</architecture>

<selected_context>
AGENTS.md: HH-first terminology contract, `phase3_v1` default, and benchmark fairness rule that `cx_proxy_total` is the primary hardware-cost axis while wall time is secondary.
README.md: warm-start chain and benchmark language; explicitly states `hh_hva_ptw` warm start, `paop_lf_std` depth-0 core, and matched-family replay with `full_meta` fallback.
MATH/Math.md: formal definitions for staged HH pool composition, mode-specific selector behavior (`legacy` vs `phase1_v1` vs `phase2_v1` / `phase3_v1`), measurement burden terms, and `simple_v1` / `full_v2` cost-aware scoring vocabulary.
MATH/IMPLEMENT_SOON.md: intended curriculum and replay semantics: seed -> core -> residual enrichment, `full_meta` admission as controlled exception layer, lifetime weighting of repeated-evaluation costs, and energy-drop-first stage transitions.
pipelines/run_guide.md: runbook-level fairness vocabulary including headline accuracy metric, hardware-oriented proxy budgets, compare-policy, and explicit mention of Pareto / best-by-budget outputs.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_staged_cli_args.py: staged HH control surface for warm, ADAPT, replay, dynamics, and budget knobs.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_staged_workflow.py: resolved staged defaults and scaled budgets; replay defaults to `match_adapt` with `full_meta` fallback, and replay continuation mode inherits ADAPT mode by default.
pipelines/hardcoded/adapt_pipeline.py: authoritative staged ADAPT mode resolution, staged stop-policy defaults (`drop_floor=5e-4`, `drop_patience=3`, `drop_min_depth=12` for staged HH), and HH pool-family construction including `paop_lf_std` and `full_meta`.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_scoring.py: actual scoring module defining compile-cost, measurement-cache, novelty, curvature, and compatibility terms used in staged continuation ranking.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_types.py: data model for `CandidateFeatures`, measurement-plan/cache stats, compile-cost estimates, replay plans, and replay telemetry.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_stage_control.py: plateau / trough / probing control logic for stage transitions.
pipelines/hardcoded/handoff_state_bundle.py: persisted handoff payload contract carrying exact-error, provenance, selected generators, replay contract hints, and continuation metadata.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_replay.py: freeze/unfreeze/full replay controller definitions and phase telemetry surface.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_continuation_generators.py: generator metadata, family/template IDs, and split-event bookkeeping that connect ADAPT selection to replay provenance.
pipelines/hardcoded/hh_vqe_from_adapt_family.py: `match_adapt` family resolution, fallback to `full_meta`, replay seed-policy resolution, and replay output metrics such as `abs_delta_e`, `nfev`, `nit`, and parameter count.
pipelines/exact_bench/benchmark_metrics_proxy.py: wrapper-level schema for workflow comparison rows; includes `delta_E_abs`, `nfev`, `depth_proxy`, `pool_family_proxy`, and related comparison fields.
pipelines/exact_bench/hh_l2_stage_unit_audit_workflow.py: stage-local audit surface exposing prefix gains, removal penalties, and logical unit cost metrics after a canonical staged run.
pipelines/exact_bench/hh_l2_logical_screen_workflow.py: workflow-level robustness screen over staged baseline plus replay ablations across representative HH points; useful for defining what counts as a workflow comparison row.
pipelines/exact_bench/hh_fixed_handoff_replay_optimizer_probe_workflow.py: fixed-scaffold optimizer comparison surface; isolates replay optimizer/search cost from scaffold differences.
pipelines/exact_bench/hh_full_pool_expressivity_probe_workflow.py: scaffold-free direct VQE comparison surface; isolates pool / parameterization expressivity from staged scaffold effects.
docs/reports/qiskit_circuit_report.py: proxy-cost definitions for `cx_proxy`, `sq_proxy`, `term_exp_count`, and total dynamics proxy aggregation.
pipelines/exact_bench/hh_noise_robustness_seq_report.py: established report fields for `cx_proxy_total`, `depth_proxy_total`, `wall_total_s`, `oracle_eval_s_total`, and related comparison metrics.
artifacts 1/useful/L2/20260309_plateau_v3_summary.md: concrete staged evidence; PTW replay outperforms layerwise across weak / knee / strong points, but knee/strong still have substantial `ΔE_replay`.
L2_hh_smart_replay.md: concrete replay evidence; fallback `full_meta` replay reached `abs_delta_e ≈ 9.56e-3` at replay depth 78 with `nfev=6001`, showing that deeper replay/search cost does not trivially guarantee final accuracy.
prompt-exports/2026-03-13-0010-plan-hh-sweep-experiments.md: strong example of repo-native GPT-Pro prompt-export structure.
prompt-exports/2026-03-12-2359-plan-hh-operator-pool-expansion.md: second example focused on external reasoning prompt design without prematurely changing canonical workflow defaults.
</selected_context>

<relationships>
- Canonical staged workflow is `hh_hva_ptw` warm start -> staged ADAPT -> handoff bundle -> matched-family replay. `hh_staged_workflow.py` orchestrates this chain; `adapt_pipeline.py` produces the ADAPT scaffold; `handoff_state_bundle.py` persists it; `hh_vqe_from_adapt_family.py` continues it.
- `phase3_v1` is the canonical staged HH mode, but `legacy`, `phase1_v1`, and `phase2_v1` remain explicit comparable policies. `adapt_pipeline.py`, `hh_continuation_stage_control.py`, `hh_continuation_scoring.py`, and `hh_continuation_replay.py` divide responsibility between admission/ranking logic and replay controller behavior.
- The repo already distinguishes search/discovery cost from final hardware cost. Search-side costs appear in ADAPT / replay telemetry (`nfev`, `adapt_depth`, compile-cost proxies, measurement-cache stats); final hardware/runtime costs appear in benchmark/report fields (`cx_proxy_total`, `depth_proxy_total`, `oracle_eval_s_total`, `wall_total_s`).
- `hh_l2_stage_unit_audit_workflow.py`, `hh_l2_logical_screen_workflow.py`, `hh_fixed_handoff_replay_optimizer_probe_workflow.py`, and `hh_full_pool_expressivity_probe_workflow.py` are complementary comparison surfaces: stage contribution, workflow robustness/ablation, optimizer sensitivity under fixed scaffold, and scaffold-free expressivity. The export should treat them as evidence about different axes of the same tradeoff problem.
- Fair-comparison guidance in `AGENTS.md`, `README.md`, and `run_guide.md` already prefers hardware-oriented proxy budgets and exact-cost tie comparisons. The export should use that vocabulary when asking GPT-Pro to define Pareto fronts and dominance.
- The selected artifact summaries show that warm-start quality, final accuracy, replay depth, and search effort can trade against each other. The export should reflect that this is a multi-objective comparison problem, not a single-metric ranking.
</relationships>

<ambiguities>
The repo has strong vocabulary for state-preparation quality (`abs_delta_e`, `delta_E_abs`, `adapt_depth`, `nfev`) and strong vocabulary for downstream hardware/noisy benchmarking (`cx_proxy_total`, `depth_proxy_total`, `oracle_eval_s_total`), but it does not appear to commit a single canonical end-to-end Pareto vector for staged HH workflow comparison. The next model should ask GPT-Pro to define that comparison vector explicitly rather than assume the repo already has one.
It is genuinely ambiguous whether the user wants the Pareto front to compare only warm+ADAPT+replay workflows, or to include downstream dynamics / noisy-validation profiles as a second layer of comparison. The export should distinguish a primary workflow-space definition from any optional downstream cost/accuracy extension.
The prompt-export example files are style guides, not problem facts. The next model should borrow their structure and clarity, not their subject matter.
</ambiguities>
</user_instructions>
